When licentious rites prevail, the spirits grow ever angrier.
When the people favor shortcuts, they turn to ghosts and spirits.

Licentious rites pervade the world, corrupting customs and fostering omens of calamity—
Families are ruined, livelihoods lost.

*—The *Chongxu Jing* states:*
As benevolence and righteousness decline, the people’s nature grows thin—
The Dao cannot prevail.

*—The *Tongxuan Jing* states:*
If one listens to wise counsel and acts accordingly,
Even the foolish know to take joy in it.
If one praises the saintly virtue and noble conduct,
Even the unworthy know to emulate it.

*—The *Tongxuan Jing* states:*
Those who delight in the Great Dao are many,
Yet those who practice it are few;
Those who aspire to it are many,
Yet those who truly walk it are few.
Only the wise fear this.

*—The *Chongxu Jing* states:*
If the Dao does not prevail,
A single kingdom may yet endure as in years past—
But how can the world and future generations endure?

The Great Dao is most simple,
*—The *Tongxuan Jing* states:*
The Great Dao is broad and easy—
It lies not far from the self.
Seek it near, yet return empty-handed.
The people love shortcuts.

*—The *Tongxuan Jing* states:*
The people greatly favor perverse shortcuts,
Turning to ghosts and spirits.
Licentious rites prevail, the spirits grow ever angrier.

*—The *Dongling Jing* states:*
The foundation of governance lies in securing the people.
If the times are not oppressive,
Yet one seizes upon laborious projects—
This is called great calamity.

*—The *Chongxu Jing* states:*
Qi and Lu abound in ingenuity,
With skilled artisans in earth and wood.

*—The *Dongling Jing* states:*
Fields lie overgrown—
People abandon essential pursuits for trivial ones.

In ancient times, the sage-kings governed by first attending to agriculture.
When the people tilled the land, they were simple,
And simplicity made them easy to guide—
Thus the borders were secure.

When the people turned to farming, they became youthful,
Youthful, they held less to private affection and more to public law.

*—The *Tongxuan Jing* discusses the laws of Shennong:*
If men of prime strength do not plow,
There will be those who starve in the world;
If women of childbearing age do not weave,
There will be those who freeze in the world.
Thus the Emperor himself plowed,
And the Empress herself wove—
Setting an example for the world.

Therefore, those who till do not toil excessively,
For they have no means to sustain life;
Those who weave do not labor excessively,
For they have no means to clothe the body.
When food and clothing are abundant,
Deceit and perversity do not arise.

To preserve the essentials of the seasons,
One must reduce unnecessary pursuits.
*—The *Dongling Jing* states:*
Agriculture yields food, artisans yield tools, merchants yield goods—
Grain is the people’s Heaven.
Thus, when a sage-king arises, he prioritizes agriculture.
If a king does not prioritize agriculture,
He abandons the people—
What kingdom can he then rule?

*—The *Tongxuan Jing* states:*
The sage-king enriches his people,
The conqueror enriches his land,
The endangered state enriches its historians,
The well-governed state finds sufficiency,
The doomed state suffers from empty granaries—
Thus it is said: *When the ruler has no burdens, the people prosper naturally.*

The foundation of sufficiency lies in not seizing the seasons.

*—The *Nanhua Jing* (Zhuangzi) states:*
In the latter age, what the people delight in
Are fine garments and beautiful colors,
Which confuse their minds and make them forget their duties—
This is called chaos.

*—The *Nanhua Jing* states:*
To teach the people’s customs,
Clothing should be plain, belts simple—
Modest and unadorned.

*—The *Nanhua Jing* (Zhuangzi) recounts how Zhuangzi admonished King Zhao of Yan for his love of swords:*
Zhuangzi said: *I have three swords—
One for the Son of Heaven, one for the feudal lords, one for the commoner.*
The king said: *I wish to hear of these three swords.*
Zhuangzi replied: *There is the sword of the Son of Heaven,
The sword of the feudal lords,
And the sword of the commoner.*
*Now, Your Majesty holds the position of the Son of Heaven,
Yet you delight in the sword of the commoner—
I humbly fear this for Your Majesty.*
The king then had the swords drawn and presented to him,
And the royal attendants served him food three times.
Zhuangzi said: *Your Majesty, remain seated and composed—
The matter of the swords is now complete.*
Thus, King Wen did not leave his palace for three months,
And all the swordsmasters perished in their homes.

*—The *Nanhua Jing* states:*
In the latter age, what the people delight in
Are rich flavors and music,
Which confuse their minds and make them forget their duties—
This is called chaos.

*—The *Nanhua Jing* states:*
To hoard wealth and take comfort in it,
To covet power and exhaust it,
To accumulate goods and seek profit—
This is called thievish arrogance.

*—The *Nanhua Jing* states:*
All these seven evils
Are the world’s greatest harms.
Yet people forget them and fail to discern—
Their desires sever from their bodies, yet they still covet—
Is this not delusion?

*—The *Chongxu Jing* states:*
When teaching is clear above and transformation spreads below,
The people have a sense of shame—
Why would there be thieves?
Thus, when governance aligns with the natural order,
Bandits flee and hide.

*—The *Tongxuan Jing* states:*
The foundation of pure transformation lies in rejecting artifice.

*—The *Nanhua Jing* states:*
Cunning, extravagance, and superficiality
Are insufficient to stabilize the world—
This is not the Dao.

**Chapter Fifty-Four: The Unshakable Builder**

*—The *Tongxuan Jing* records Wenzi asking:*
Master, your words say that without virtue and the Dao,
One cannot govern the world.
Yet in ancient times, kings inherited their predecessors’ legacies—
Some ruled without virtue, yet their ages endured without calamity.
How is this possible?

Laozi replied:
From the Son of Heaven down to the commoner,
Each lives their own life—
Yet life varies in depth.
The world at times sees ruined families and fallen states,
All due to the absence of virtue and the Dao.

If one remains ever vigilant, day and night,
Striving with fear and caution,
Guarding diligently without fail—
Then disaster is averted.

But if one indulges in desires and neglects duty,
Unable to guard diligently,
Then ruin comes without warning.

If Jie and Zhou had followed the Dao and cultivated virtue,
Even if Tang and Wu were wise,
They would have had no means to establish their deeds.

In ancient times, those who built well were unshaken,
Those who guarded well were unlost—
Thus their descendants continued sacrifices without interruption,
Their virtue never severed,
And the world endured for generations.

Those who build well are unshaken—
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says: In ancient times, those who built well were unshaken,
Meaning that the cultivation of virtue in building was without action or favor,
And they upheld modesty and frugality.

*The Scripture of the Numinous Spirit* says: King Wen acted with tranquility in advance and retreat,
And Heaven would surely assist him—
His fortune was divined as lasting thirty generations.

Those who embrace well are not abandoned—
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says: In ancient times, the sage-kings dwelled in great fullness yet did not overflow,
And in lofty nobility yet did not grow proud.
Dwelling in great fullness yet not overflowing,
This is how they long preserved their wealth;
Residing in lofty nobility yet not growing proud,
This is how they long preserved their honor.

*The Scripture of the Numinous Spirit* says: The virtue of King Wen was such that Jie could not harm it.
His longevity was foretold in dreams—
Seven hundred years, a command from Heaven.
Thus his descendants continued sacrifices without interruption.

*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says: Riches and honor never depart from their person,
And blessings extend to their offspring—
This was indeed the ancient royal Dao.
Cultivate it in oneself, and its virtue becomes true;
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* [*The Chapter of Subtle Clarity*] says:
Commoners and scholars alike, if they follow the Dao,
Will preserve their own lives—
Thus it is said: Cultivate it in oneself,
And its virtue becomes true.

*The Scripture of the South Flowering* says:
In antiquity, the five offices fulfilled their distinct duties,
And commoners governed themselves and cultivated their virtue—
This was the beauty of governance.

Cultivate it in the family, and its virtue becomes abundant;
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
In ancient times, great officials with the Dao
Did not lose their families—
Thus it is said: Cultivate it in the family,
And its virtue becomes abundant.

*The Scripture of the South Flowering* says:
Great officials governed themselves and cultivated their virtue—
This was the beauty of governance.

Cultivate it in the village, and its virtue becomes enduring;
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
In ancient times, prefects and counties with the Dao
Did not lose their villages—
Thus it is said: Cultivate it in the village,
And its virtue becomes enduring.

Cultivate it in the state, and its virtue becomes plentiful;
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
In ancient times, the feudal lords with the Dao
Did not lose their states—
Thus it is said: Cultivate it in the state,
And its virtue becomes plentiful.

*The Scripture of the South Flowering* says:
Feudal lords governed themselves and cultivated their virtue—
This was the beauty of governance.

Cultivate it in the world, and its virtue becomes universal.
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
In ancient times, the Son of Heaven with the Dao
Long held dominion over the world—
Thus it is said: Cultivate it in the world,
And its virtue becomes universal.

*The Scripture of the South Flowering* says:
The Son of Heaven governed himself and cultivated his virtue—
This was the beauty of governance.

Thus, observe oneself with oneself—
*The Scripture of the South Flowering* says:
In the latter ages, if the five do not cultivate,
No greater loss can there be.
Commoners not cultivating, lose their own lives.
Observe the family with the family—
*The Scripture of the South Flowering* says:
Great officials not cultivating, lose their families.
Observe the village with the village—
*The Scripture of the South Flowering* says:
Prefects and counties not cultivating, lose their villages.
Observe the state with the state—
*The Scripture of the South Flowering* says:
Feudal lords not cultivating, lose their states.
Observe the world with the world—
*The Scripture of the South Flowering* says:
The Son of Heaven not cultivating, loses his world.

How do I know the world is thus?
By this.

*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
Not losing the root of the state lies in the virtue of guarding well—
Those who do not increase its substance yet expand its reach are ruined,
Those who do not broaden its foundation yet raise its height are overturned.

No burden is heavier than the beams,
No governance of the state is heavier than virtue.

*The Chapter of Embracing Virtue’s Depth* [This chapter, *The Scripture of the South Flowering* [*The Chapter of the Horse’s Hoof*], says:]
In the upper antiquity, the age of the Perfected Dao and Supreme Virtue,
Its people were like infants, pure as newborns.
Their actions were simple and unadorned,
They did not know east or west;
Their vision was unclouded,
They did not know darkness or light.

In that time, birds and beasts gathered in flocks,
Grasses and trees grew in abundance—
Thus, birds and beasts could be tethered and led about,
Yet they did not harm people;
The nests of crows and magpies could be climbed and observed,
Yet they did not injure people.

Beasts could not prey upon them,
Not because their virtue was thin—
Rather, they discerned safety and danger,
Settled in peace with calamity and fortune,
And were cautious in their choices—
None could harm them,
For this was the result of embracing virtue.

*The Scripture of the Void and the Primordial* says:
In the age of the Great Beginning,
Birds and beasts dwelled with humans,
And moved alongside them.
In the time of the Five Emperors and Three Kings,
Birds and beasts began to scatter in alarm.

By the latter ages,
Birds and beasts hid and fled, escaping their hardships.

*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
In the latter ages, the Dao declines and virtue thins—
Humans become the robbers,
And birds, beasts, insects, and serpents all harm people—
Thus, iron is cast and blades are forged to repel their dangers.

In the upper antiquity, virtue was profound,
Their nature was like that of a newborn babe—
Without the hearts of harm or gain,
They were simple and long-lived.

The depth of embracing virtue—
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
In ancient times, the treatment of the Perfected Ones
Was to embrace virtue and hold the Dao,
To be serene and content without arrogance,
And thus attain harmony—
Robbers and thieves did not act,
For this was the result of embracing virtue.

*The Scripture of the Void and the Primordial* says:
Embrace their virtue, and they harmonize with all things created.
Like a newborn babe—
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
In ancient times, the age of supreme virtue,
Its people were like infants, pure as those three months old,
Unknowing of harm or gain—
Robbers and thieves did not act,
For this was the governance of embracing virtue.

*The Scripture of the South Flowering* says:
Does the *Scripture of Vitality* teach the art of longevity?
All day long they move, yet do not know where they go,
They dwell, yet do not know what they do—
Their bodies are like withered branches of wood.
If such is their state,
Then calamity will not come,
Nor fortune arrive—
Calamity and fortune are nonexistent,
For evil men and malevolent things cannot harm them.

Poisonous creatures do not sting—
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* [*The Chapter of Pure Sincerity*] says:
In ancient times, the sage-king Fuxi ruled the world,
His virtue gave life yet did not kill.
At that time, even venomous serpents
Held their tail-poisons in concealment,
And their sting-poisons were hidden—
They did not bite people,
For this was the result of embracing virtue.

Fierce beasts did not attack—
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
In ancient times, the sage-king Fuxi ruled the world,
His virtue gave life yet did not kill.
At that time, even fierce beasts
Had their claws and teeth—
Yet the herds of running beasts could be tethered and led,
And they did not harm people,
For this was the result of embracing virtue.

Birds of prey did not strike.
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
In ancient times, the sage-king Fuxi ruled the world,
His virtue gave life yet did not kill.
At that time, even birds and beasts had their claws and talons—
Yet the nests of flying birds could be approached and explored,
And they did not harm people,
For this was the result of embracing virtue.

Bones were weak, sinews supple, yet their grasp was firm.
*The South华 Scripture* says:
The child held all day, yet his hands did not tire,
His virtue was one—
He gazed all day, yet his eyes did not strain,
For his mind was not outward.
This was the virtue of the Perfect Man.

Unknowing of male and female union yet life arose—
The essence was supreme.
*The South华 Scripture* says:
The child moved without purpose,
His body like a withered tree’s branch,
His heart like dead ashes—
This was the essence supreme.

*The Scripture of Void and Emptiness* says:
The infant brother’s wholeness.

Crying all day, yet his throat did not grow hoarse—
Harmony was supreme.
*The South华 Scripture* says:
The child cried all day, yet his throat did not grow hoarse,
For harmony was supreme.

To know harmony is to know constancy.
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* [*The Chapter of Lower Virtue*] says:
In the ancient times, life was cherished,
Life was valued above gain—
No harm came to the spirit,
And longevity was granted.
Thus it is said: To know harmony is to know constancy.

*The Scripture of Void and Emptiness* says:
In ancient times, the infant’s nature was pure,
Qi focused, will unified—
This was harmony supreme.
Nothing injured it,
No virtue surpassed it.

To know constancy is to know clarity.
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
Later generations valued gain above life,
This is called excessive harm.
Those who harm themselves thus have no longevity.
Thus it is said: To know constancy is to know clarity.

To benefit life is auspicious.
*The Scripture of Void and Emptiness* says:
In their youth, they were delicate and skilled,
Their fame and reputation were exaggerated in the world.
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
To benefit life is auspicious.

To let the heart command qi is strength.
*The Scripture of Void and Emptiness* says:
In their youthful vigor, blood and qi overflowed,
Desires and thoughts filled them,
They were assailed by external things,
And their virtue thus declined.
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
To let the heart command qi is strength.

When things are strong, they age.
*The Scripture of Void and Emptiness* says:
In their old age, desires and thoughts grew soft,
Their bodies neared rest,
Nothing could precede them.
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
The spirit, will, and qi—
When still, they grow daily stronger;
When agitated, they waste and age.
This is called *not-Dao*.
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
Some die young, not by fate but by self-harm,
Neglecting their bodies, letting illness kill them.
Only the tranquil and content can manifest virtue,
Thus, to act against the Dao is not virtue,
And none can endure long—
The world has none who live long against the Dao.
Not-Dao brings early death.
Not-Dao brings early death.

*The Scripture of Void and Emptiness* says:
In death, they return to stillness,
And return to their origin.

**Chapter Fifty-Six: The Silent Sage**
This chapter of *The South华 Scripture* speaks:
The ancient Dao and virtue were obscured by those who followed the various schools,
The Nine Flows heard their heterodox winds and rejoiced in them,
Using rigid rules to correct themselves,
To address the world’s urgencies,
They destroyed the ancient Dao and virtue,
And did not align with the former kings.

To govern the world and nourish the people—
What is this different from tending horses?
One removes only what harms the horses,
And those who harm the people.

The wise scholar without thought and contemplation is not content,
The eloquent scholar without discourse is not content,
The discerning scholar without judgment is not content—
All are constrained by things,
And have lost their Dao.

Those who attract the world’s favor rise in court,
The common scholars are honored in the halls,
The strong are praised for their strength,
The brave are celebrated for their daring,
The martial are delighted in war,
The ascetics cherish their names,
The legalists expand their governance,
The ritualists respect their forms,
The benevolent are esteemed for their connections.

Without accumulated wealth, the greedy grieve,
Without unrivaled power, the ambitious sorrow—
Those who rely on external things
Take pleasure in change and opportunity,
And cannot avoid causing harm.
The Nine Flows obstruct the Dao,
And learning becomes chaotic.

The sage does not speak.
*The South华 Scripture* says:
The ancient scholars did nothing, thought nothing, contemplated nothing,
And thus came to know the Dao.
The sage does not speak.
Those who speak do not know.

To block the mouth,
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* [*The Chapter of Lower Virtue*] says:
The ancient scholars blocked their mouths,
Their speech was cautious,
Great eloquence seemed stammering.

To close the gate,
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
The ancient scholars closed their gates,
Silent yet wise,
Great skill seemed clumsy.

To blunt the sharp,
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
The ancient scholars blunted the sharp,
Abandoning vigor and ambition,
No weapons were needed.

To resolve the tangled,
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
The ancient scholars resolved the tangled,
There was no strife or disorder,
And the world was at peace.

To harmonize their light,
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
The ancient scholars harmonized their light,
There was no resentment or defiance.

To blend with the dust,
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
The ancient scholars blended with the dust,
There was no contention or grievance.
This is called *Mystic Unity*.
*The South华 Scripture* says:
Yan Hui said:
To abandon limbs and senses,
To discard form and wisdom,
To merge with the Great Communion—
This is called *Sitting-Forgetting*.
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
All things are mystically unified,
Neither this nor that.

Thus it cannot be approached or avoided,
*The South华 Scripture* says:
The benevolent are esteemed for their connections,
The discerning scholar without judgment is not content.

It cannot be distanced or drawn near,
*The South华 Scripture* says:
The ritualists respect their forms,
The wise scholar without thought is not content.

It cannot be used for gain,
*The South华 Scripture* says:
The eloquent scholar without discourse is not content.

《The Scripture of Perfected Mystery》 says:
The resentful are contrary to *virtue/power*.
Strife is the source of human disorder.
To employ dark schemes contrary to *virtue/power* to suppress human disorder is the height of perversity.
One cannot bring calamity upon others unless they are already calamitous.
It cannot be used to cause harm;

*The South华 Scripture* says:
The bold and courageous delight in slaughter,
The martial scholars delight in war.

*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
Weapons are cruel instruments.
To delight in using cruel instruments to suppress human disorder is the height of perversity.
One cannot bring calamity upon others unless they are already calamitous.

It cannot be esteemed for its own sake;
*The South华 Scripture* says:
The noble do not take honor as their ease,
Nor rely on power to be revered.

Without glorying in *Mystic Unity*,
There is no *Daoist* resentment from Heaven.
Without being held in contempt,
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
One need not depend on wealth to be rich,
Nor fear disgrace as perilous.

Without being shamed by poverty,
There is no human censure.
Thus, one is held in highest esteem by the world.

*The South华 Scripture* says:
In ancient times, the sudden outburst of ambition was condemned.
Honor, wealth, high rank, splendid appearance, fame, and profit—
These six things are the sudden outburst of ambition.
If the heart remains unmoved,
Then one is upright.
Being upright,
One attains emptiness, tranquility, and non-action,
Yet nothing remains undone.

*The Collected Commentaries on the Four Children of the Daoist True Scripture* concludes Volume Seven,
Begins Volume Eight.

**Chapter Fifty-Seventh: Governing by the Dao**

*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* speaks:
In the Spring and Autumn era, the Warring States’ ambition gave rise to cunning and deceit, while theft and banditry flourished. The ruler and ruled harbored mutual resentment, and decrees failed to take hold.

When waters grow turbid, fish scatter;
When governance grows harsh, the people rebel.
Excessive prohibitions breed defiance below,
Excessive demands spawn contention.
Thus, applying the remedy of boiling water to boiling water only intensifies the heat—
One who understands *wuwei* as the foundation of governance knows to remove the fire itself.

Therefore it is said:
*"I practice non-action, yet the people transform themselves;
I cherish stillness, yet the people align themselves."*

The Five Hegemons’ reliance on arms and punishments bred bandits and chaos.

**Governing by the Dao,**
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* (□ *On Rites Above*) states:
To govern by the Dao, first establish policies that cannot be overcome,
Then seek victory over adversaries.
To attack a disordered state before it is pacified
Is like responding to fire with fire or water with water—
Opposites cannot govern one another;
This is called *increasing disorder*.

**Employing the Unconventional in Warfare,**
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
To employ the unconventional in warfare,
One must make the strange appear strange.
The unconventional in stillness appears agitated,
The unconventional in order appears chaotic,
The unconventional in abundance appears starved,
The unconventional in ease appears labored.

The interplay of the unconventional and the conventional
Is like the clash of water, fire, metal, and wood—
Wherever it turns, it prevails.

**Conquering the World Without Conflict,**
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
The ancient sage-rulers conquered the world without conflict.
How do I know this is so?
By this:
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
Excessive affairs are difficult to govern,
Harsh laws are difficult to enforce.
When taboos proliferate,
*The Scripture of the Cavern Spirit* says:
When customs overflow with taboos,
Emotions stagnate, and the world grows rigid;
When customs lack taboos,
Suppression and release flow freely, and joyous communication thrives.
Yet the people grow ever poorer.

When sharp weapons abound,
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
Heavy armor and sharp blades cannot be relied upon for strength.
When the state grows ever more corrupt,
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
When rulers favor martial prowess and incite the people to contention,
The state faces endless calamity, and rebellion will surely follow.

When cunning and skill proliferate,
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
When cleverness and ingenuity flourish, strange things arise.
*The South华 Scripture* says:
Those who excel in cleverness, wisdom, and saintly virtue—
I alone consider myself lost among them.
When those who rely on cunning to overcome strength become too numerous,
Excessive precision will inevitably breed unworthy hearts in response,
Yet they remain unaware.

When laws and decrees multiply,
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
The art of governance lies not in eloquence.
When laws and decrees multiply, thieves and bandits thrive.
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
Cunning and deceit take root, and banditry spreads.
Thus the sages say:
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
Laws may kill the unfilial, yet cannot make one filial;
Punishments may deter thieves, yet cannot instill honesty.
In the latter ages, when the world fears punishment and dares not steal—
Is this not inferior to the ancient purity where no thief’s heart arose?
Thus, applying the remedy of boiling water to boiling water only intensifies the heat—
One who understands *wuwei* as the foundation of governance knows to remove the fire itself.

Therefore the sages say:
*"I practice non-action, yet the people transform themselves;
I desire nothing, yet the people return to simplicity."*

*"I practice non-action, yet the people transform themselves,"*
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* (□ *On the Origin of the Dao*) says:
*"I practice non-action, yet the people transform themselves,
Thus the ruler practices non-action, and the people transform themselves."*

*"I engage in no affairs, yet the people grow rich,"*
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
*"I engage in no affairs, yet the people grow rich,
Thus the ruler engages in no affairs, and the people grow rich."*

*"I cherish stillness, yet the people align themselves,"*
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
*"I cherish stillness, yet the people align themselves,
Thus the ruler cherishes stillness, and the people align themselves."*

*"I desire nothing, yet the people return to simplicity."*
*The Scripture of Perfected Mystery* says:
*"I desire nothing, yet the people return to simplicity,
Thus the ruler desires nothing, and the people return to simplicity."*

---

**Chapter Fifty-Eighth: The Obscure Governance**

This chapter, from *The South华 Scripture* (□ *On the Redundant Thumb*), speaks:
Since the Three Sovereigns, how have the world’s rituals of benevolence and righteousness, its rules and measures, its hooks and cords, become so clamorous?
They carve and polish what is naturally upright in humanity.

Moreover, the Three Sovereigns relied on hooks and cords, rules and measures, to straighten what was already straight—
This was to chisel away at their natural uprightness.
They bound with cords and sealed with glue to solidify what was already firm—
This was to encroach upon their innate virtue.

They bent and folded rites and music,
They stifled and smothered benevolence and righteousness,
To pacify the world’s hearts—
This was to lose their natural order.

When governance is scrutinizing, the people grow weary;
In ancient times, the world had its natural order:
The crooked were not straightened with hooks,
The straight were not measured with cords,
The round were not circumscribed with compasses,
The square were not checked with rulers,
The separated were not glued together,
The bound were not restrained with ropes.

Thus the world spontaneously gave birth to all things, yet knew not how it came to be;
All things naturally attained their place, yet knew not how it happened.

When governance is obscure, the people are pure.
This principle is unchanging from ancient to modern—
It cannot be diminished.
Then why do benevolence and righteousness cling so tightly,
Like glue and cords, to wander between virtue and the Dao?

If governance is overly analytical,
It is like recklessly digging through walls to cultivate weeds—
Laboring without fruit.

The hair was simply unbound and combed,
The rice was merely counted and cooked—
Yet how could such modest means suffice to save the world?

The Three Sovereigns governed by discerning the people’s hardships.
When governance is obscure, the people are pure.
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* (上礼篇) says:
The waters of Ying are ten *ren* deep, yet they do not receive filth.
Jade and stone within reveal their forms without—
Not because they are not thick or clear,
But fish, turtles, dragons, and serpents do not dwell there.
No grains grow upon barren stone,
No deer roam the bald mountains—
For there is no shelter or refuge.

When governance is obscure, the people are pure.
When governance is scrutinizing, the people grow weary.
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
Later rulers govern with severity as discernment,
With harshness as clarity,
With cruelty as loyalty,
With scheming as merit.
Such rulers are like broad leather—
The wider they stretch, the more they tear.

When governance is scrutinizing, the people grow weary.
Calamity is the reverse of fortune.
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
Benefit and harm share a gate,
Calamity and fortune share a neighbor.
Thus it is said: Calamity is the reverse of fortune,
Fortune is the reverse of calamity.

The Three Sovereigns’ wisdom was shallow,
Then they relied on scrutiny.
Those who rely on scrutiny
Take the good from below to serve above, yet are deceived.
To scrutinize the traces of blades and brushes—
They know not the Way of *wuwei*,
They know the roots of chaos.
To be scrutinizing brings chaos,
Corrupts customs,
And breeds the winds of ruined states.
Who knows its ultimate end?
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
Calamity, fortune, benefit, harm—
None but the ancient sages could truly distinguish them.
Thus it is said: Who knows its ultimate end?
Is there no right or wrong?
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
The ancients governed with righteousness and transformed with ease—
Later ages govern with deceit, and though difficult, they fail.
The right becomes the strange,
*The *Scripture of the Cavern Spirit* says:
In recent times, upright men are few.
When governance is simple, the people are pure and honest,
The common folk are virtuous—
They can be transformed, not punished.
The good becomes the monstrous.
*The *Scripture of the Cavern Spirit* says:
In recent times, the wicked are many.
When governance is burdensome and harsh, the people become deceitful.
To blame the many for their deceit—
Should you not first examine your own rectitude?
The people’s confusion has long endured.
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
Later ages take petty acts of benevolence and righteousness as their measure,
Yet those who know how to use hooks, cords, compasses, and rulers can govern men—
Without these tools, one cannot establish the square or round,
Without hooks and cords, one cannot straighten the crooked.
If the ruler relies on these tools,
The people below also harbor such scheming hearts—
They are clever devices, yet not the means to govern.

Thus the sage
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
Murky waters choke the fish,
Harsh governance breeds chaos in the people.
When the ruler’s desires multiply, the people’s deceit multiplies,
When the ruler is troubled, the people become unsettled.
Not knowing the root of *wuwei* for one person,
They seek to remedy it with the superficial laws of governance—
How different is this from digging canals to stop the flow of water,
Or embracing firewood to extinguish flames,
Yet calling it an increase?
Thus, to stop the boiling with a ladle only makes it worse—
He who knows the true method of governance removes the fire itself.

Therefore the sage governs with simplicity and achieves order,
Seeks few things and finds abundance,
For what he cultivates is the root.

Square yet not cutting,
Modest yet not stingy,
Straight yet not domineering,
Brilliant yet not dazzling—
These four, truly cultivated, are the Way of proper governance.

Square yet not cutting,
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* (道德篇) says:
The ancients governed with the Dao—
Square yet not cutting, and the people naturally conform.
*The *South Flower Sutra* says:
The ancients had the constant Way—
The square was not measured with a ruler.

Modest yet not stingy,
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
The ancients nourished with virtue—
Modest yet not stingy, and the people submit.
*The *South Flower Sutra* says:
The ancients had the constant Way—
The round was not circumscribed with a compass.

Straight yet not domineering,
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
Without adding force,
Straight yet not domineering, and the people suffice in frugality.
*The *South Flower Sutra* says:
The ancients had the constant Way—
The crooked were not straightened with hooks,
The straight were not measured with cords.

Brilliant yet not dazzling.
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
Without displaying virtue,
Brilliant yet not dazzling, and the people remain pure and honest.
*The *South Flower Sutra* says:
The ancient sages did not ponder or premeditate,
They shone yet did not dazzle.

**Chapter Fifty-Nine: Governing Men and Serving Heaven**
This chapter of the *South Flower Sutra* speaks:
Though noble as the Son of Heaven, they did not use their nobility to domineer over others;
Though wealthy with all under heaven, they did not use their riches to mock others.
Rich and noble yet frugal—
This is truly virtue.
When the people are frugal, the state endures.

Governing men and serving Heaven,
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
The ruler’s relation to the people is like the foundation to a city.
A thick foundation makes the city firm,
A wealthy people make the state prosperous.
None surpass frugality.
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
The ancient sages governed with the Dao—
Frugality and modesty were seen as scarcity,
For seeing scarcity, they could achieve abundance,
Thus enduring long.

Only frugality,
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
The ruler’s Way lies in frugality to preserve life—
This is called early cultivation of virtue.
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
Frugality prevents the people from hunger.
Early cultivation is called accumulating virtue—
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
Accumulating virtue makes kingship,
Accumulating stones makes mountains,
Accumulating water makes rivers.
Without accumulation, nothing is achieved.
Accumulating virtue without limit,
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
The skilled ruler accumulates virtue,
And the people can be employed.
Without limit, none know its end,
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
The ancient sages dared not indulge in extravagance,
Guarding frugality, thus enduring long.
None know its end—this is how one establishes a state.
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
The ancient sages did not dare to be extravagant or arrogant,
Guarding frugality, thus enduring long.

The mother of a lasting state—
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
The people are the root of a state.
Frugality is the foundation of humanity.
This is called deep-rooted and firmly anchored—
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
The ruler’s possession of the people is like a tree’s possession of its roots.
The greater the tree, the deeper its roots and the firmer its trunk.
This is the Dao of enduring life and long reign.

*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
The people are the root and foundation,
The state is the branches and leaves.
When the root and foundation are deep and robust,
The branches and leaves flourish and excel.

**Chapter Sixty: Governing Great States**
This chapter from *The South华经* speaks:
*My teacher!* *My teacher!*
He nourishes all things without excess,
His blessings extend to all ages without partiality,
His life surpasses the ancient sages without boasting of longevity,
He encompasses heaven and earth,
Molds myriad forms without artifice—
This is called *Heaven’s Harmony*.

The ancient sages who understood *Heaven’s Harmony*
Had no celestial grievance,
No human censure,
No burden from things,
No reproach from spirits.

The Dao does not harm the people,
And the world finds harmony and joy,
In accord with the people’s harmony.

Governing great states—
*The *South华经* says:
The ancient sages were clear in the virtue/power of heaven and earth’s non-action,
This is called the great lineage, the great root,
Rooted in the Dao,
In harmony with heaven.

In harmony with heaven—
This is called *Heaven’s Harmony*.
Thus, those who know *Heaven’s Harmony*
Have no celestial grievance.

If one cooks a small delicacy—
*The *South华经* says:
The sages’ non-action
Balances and harmonizes the world,
In accord with humanity—
This is called *The People’s Harmony*.
Thus, those who know *The People’s Harmony*
Have no human censure.

With the Dao to govern the world—
*The *South华经* says:
The ancient sages’ life was in accord with heaven’s movement,
Their death was in accord with nature’s transformation.
In stillness, they aligned with the yin’s virtue/power,
In motion, they rode the waves of the yang—
This is called *in harmony with heaven*.
*In harmony with heaven*—
This is called *Heaven’s Harmony*.
Thus, those who know *Heaven’s Harmony*
Have no burden from things.

Their spirits are not numinous—
*The *South华经* says:
The ancient sages—
In action, they were heaven,
In stillness, they were earth.
With a single, steadfast heart, they ruled the world,
Their spirits did not vex,
Their souls did not weary,
With a single, steadfast heart, all things submitted—
This is called *in accord with humanity*.
*In accord with humanity*—
This is called *The People’s Harmony*.
Thus, those who know *The People’s Harmony*
Have no reproach from spirits.

It is not that their spirits are not numinous—
*The *South华经* says:
The ancient sages spoke of emptiness and stillness,
Extending it to heaven and earth,
Permeating all things—
This is called *Heaven’s Harmony*,
*In harmony with heaven*.
Their numinous transformations did not harm the people—
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* [□ *Precision of Sincerity*] says:
The highest numinous transformations,
The people have no complaint.
Yet when numinous transformations have complaint—
It is not that their numinous transformations harm the people—
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
The numinous transformations of the wordless Dao
Carry all without complaint,
Not harming the numinous nature of those who possess the Dao’s spirit.
The sages also do not harm the people.

*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
The people are governed without action,
Action brings harm.
Governing without action—
The two do not harm each other,
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
Those who act
Cannot truly be without action,
Those who cannot be without action
Cannot truly act—
This harms the people.
Thus, virtue/power returns to its source.

*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
The ancient sages who knew *Heaven’s Harmony*
With a single, steadfast heart
Nourished the world without action—
And the world found harmony and joy.

**Chapter Sixty-One: Great States as the Lowly Flow**
This chapter from *The Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* speaks:
In the Warring States era, the public lords and marquises treated a single state as their own,
Their *qi* was abundant yet their resolve was strong,
The powerful used arms to invade the weak,
The weak defied and undermined the strong,
Clinging to their weapons with rigid resolve,
Creating strife and fostering resentment,
For long they did not achieve harmony—
And the world fell into great disorder.

Thus, when states are bound in harmony and stillness,
And arms are laid down without contention,
The world attains great peace.

Great states are the lowly flow of the world—
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
Hence, the Dao does not triumph through rigid strength,
Nor does it gain through greedy competition.
Victory lies in the world’s spontaneous submission,
Gain lies in the world’s accord with you.
Softness and weakness bring victory,
Ren and righteousness bring gain.
The world’s receptive feminine—
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
The ancient sages acted as the world’s receptive feminine,
Thus they could endure long.

The receptive feminine constantly triumphs through stillness over the masculine—
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
The Dao of victory through arms
Awaits disorder with governance,
Awaits motion with stillness,
Awaits the masculine with the receptive feminine—
One must not act first.
Stillness is the lowly way—
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
Thus the sages grasp the feminine and receptive,
And so can establish their masculine and strong.
Advancing with the receptive feminine,
Their virtue/power and deeds do not decline—
This is the way of heaven.

Guard the Dao of stillness,
Restrain the feminine’s resolve,
With softness and weakness, find peace in stillness.
Thus, great states submit to small states and take them—
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
To govern with greatness over smallness,
This is called *altering humanity*.
Small states submit to great states and take them—
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
To offend with smallness against greatness,
This is called *defying heaven*.

Thus, sometimes one submits to take—
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
The small and weak have the Dao,
They gain without contention.
Sometimes one submits and takes—
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
The strong and great have the Dao,
They conquer without battle.

Great states seek only to nurture and embrace others—
*The *Vacuous and Pure Communiqué* says:
Small states I will cherish,
If they rely on arms and authority,
Their extinction is imminent.

Small states seek only to serve others—
*The *Vacuous and Pure Communiqué* says:
Great states I will serve—
This is the path to seeking peace.
Both find what they desire—
*The *South华经* says:

To renew the world, to disband armies and rest the soldiers,
to cherish and nourish all kin,
and to share in ancestral sacrifices—
this is the conduct of the Sage and worthy scholar,
and the longing of all under heaven.

Thus, the great should act as the humble.

*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
The Sages of ancient times, who were lowly, modest, and pure,
saw what was beneath them.
By seeing what was beneath them, they could uphold their loftiness,
while the proud could not stand.
The Dao/Way is the deepest mystery of all things—**Chapter Sixty-Two**
This chapter of *The South华经* speaks: The governance of the ancient Sages
was always external before internal.
Without action, they were clear and tranquil,
they aligned themselves and then acted,
and firmly accomplished their tasks—
that was all.

Later generations of rulers
established laws and standards by which to judge others,
who dared not disobey and thus transform themselves—
this was to deceive virtue/power.

In governing the world,
it is like crossing the sea or digging rivers
and commanding mosquitoes to carry mountains—
laboring without gain,
not as good as the Three Sovereigns* following the Way of non-action,
which governs without labor.
Advancing the Dao/Way requires no labor.

The Dao/Way,
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
gives birth to all things,
rests in yin and yang,
transforms into the four seasons,
divides into the five phases,*
and each finds its place—
this is called the Dao/Way.
The deepest mystery of all things,
*The *South华经* says:
The Dao/Way is the source from which all things arise.

The treasure of the virtuous,
*The *South华经* says:
Moreover, the Dao/Way—
those who lose it perish,
those who act against it fail.
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
Nothing is easier under heaven than doing good.
What is called doing good
is to remain still and without action,
to follow one’s nature and discard excess,
to avoid all enticements and temptations,
to follow one’s nature and preserve truth,
to undergo no change within oneself—
thus, doing good is easy.

The safeguard of the unvirtuous,
*The *South华经* says:
Moreover, the Dao/Way—
those who lose it die,
those who act against it fail.
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
Nothing is harder under heaven than doing evil.
What is called doing evil
is to be turbulent, obscuring, and deceitful,
to be restless and greedy,
contrary to human nature—
thus, it is said that doing evil is hard.

Persuasive words can be sold,
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
First teach with the Dao/Way,
then guide with virtue/power,
to entice the good.
Noble conduct can elevate others.
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
If simple exhortation is not heeded,
then apply authority and punishment.
Why should the unvirtuous be abandoned?
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
With such strict warnings,
how could there be any unvirtuous?

Humans do not abandon humans,
things do not abandon things.
Thus, establishing the Son of Heaven,
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
The ancients established the Son of Heaven
to uphold the Dao/Way of governing the world,
to return to the root of non-action,
and to transform through emptiness and tranquility.

The ancients did not establish emperors and kings
to indulge their desires,
nor did the Sages ascend the throne
to enjoy leisure at their ease.
They made the world’s people strong to protect the weak,
many to guard the few,
the cunning to deceive the simple,
the brave to overwhelm the timid—
yet they also did not teach the clever with their cleverness,
nor distribute wealth with their wealth.
Thus, the Son of Heaven was established to harmonize them.

Setting up the Three Ministers and Nine Officials,
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
The wisdom of one person could not encompass all within the Four Seas,
so the Three Ministers and Nine Officials were appointed to assist and support them.

For isolated states and diverse customs that could not be reached by virtue/power,
the feudal lords were also established to teach and guide them.

Even with treasures of jade and rare tributes,
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
authority and influence are the chariots of the ruler.
Yu* was lean and emaciated,
Shun* was dark and withered,
Yu* had calloused hands and feet—
not that they desired wealth or craved position,
but they sought to awaken the world’s benefit
and remove the harm of all people.

From the Son of Heaven down to the common folk,
no one’s thoughts were burdened—
thus, there were none who sought sustenance without labor.

The leading four horses,
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
great ministers are the leading four horses of the ruler.
Yi Yin carried a cauldron to serve Tang*,
Lu Wang wielded an axe to enter Zhou*,
Bai Li Xi sold himself into slavery,
Guan Zhong was bound with ropes,
Mo Zi had no warm seat,
and Confucius had no heated席—
their bodies were not weary.
Thus, there were none who sought sustenance without labor.

Better to sit and advance this Dao/Way.
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
The ancients of the Three Sovereigns*
taught without descending from their halls,
yet their transformations reached the Four Seas.
They spoke no words yet moved all under heaven,
altered customs and habits,
and people transformed and became virtuous—
as if they were born that way.
Criminal punishments were insufficient to change customs,
slaughter was insufficient to stop deceit—
only divine transformation is precious.

Why was this Dao/Way so esteemed in antiquity?
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
The ancients, both ruler and subject,
engaged in few and simple matters above,
and followed easy and natural functions below—
ruler and subject did not weary of each other,
and this way endured for ages.
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Pure* says:
If the ruler clears his heart and reduces his tasks,
and the subjects revere and uphold their duties,
then Great Peace will naturally arise.

Not seeking daily to obtain,
*The *Communiqué on the Mysterious and Transcendent* says:
The ancients who were good at ruling
modeled themselves after the rivers and seas.
Rivers and seas act without effort,
yet can draw all streams to themselves.
They do not seek yet gain,
they do not act yet succeed—
the Dao/Way of heaven and earth,
complete without action,
obtained without seeking.

Does this mean crimes are pardoned?
*The *South华经* says:
In ancient times, the states that established virtue/power,
their people were simple and unrefined—
yet they governed themselves.
Thus, they were esteemed under heaven.
*The *South华经* says:
The ancients valued non-action,
non-action above,
and non-action below as well.
**Chapter Sixty-Three on Non-Action**

This chapter of *The South华经* speaks: In response to the Son of Heaven’s governance of non-action,
the House of You* did not compare to the House of Tai*.
The House of Tai* practiced non-action,
their sleep was slow and deep,
without dreams,
their waking was clear and bright,
without thought or deliberation.
Their wisdom was pure and trustworthy, not deceitful,
their virtue/power was thoroughly true, not false—
they had never yet allowed the Dao/Way to enter into inhumanity.

The House of You had action,
yet it still relied on reducing benevolence and righteousness to coerce the people’s hearts toward goodness—
yet it still gained the people’s deceit and falsehood,
and never truly cultivated a benevolent heart beyond humanity.

The ancient sages could practice the Dao/Way of non-action,
for non-action was not difficult—
non-action, *The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Non-action is non-action—
*The South华经* says:
Adrift in non-action.

Non-action in affairs is non-action—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Non-action in affairs is knowing the unknown—
*The South华经* says:
Adrift in the business of non-affairs.

Non-action in taste is non-taste—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The ancients savored the Dao without abandoning it,
while modern men abandon the Dao without savoring it.

Great and small—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The Dao of Heaven and Earth,
greatness rooted in the small,
the Dao great in its completion through the small.
The ancient sages modeled Heaven’s non-action,
softness, weakness, subtlety, and mystery—
this was seeing the small.
Seeing the small, thus they could achieve the great.

Much and little—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The Dao of Heaven and Earth,
abundance rooted in scarcity,
the Dao abundant in its completion through the little.
The ancient sages modeled Heaven’s non-action,
governing the world with the Dao,
diminishing their brilliance—
this was seeing the little.
Seeing the little, thus they could achieve the beautiful.

Repaying resentment with virtue/power—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The thicker the giving, the finer the return,
the greater the resentment, the deeper the calamity.
Sparse giving with great expectations,
nurturing resentment without calamity—
this has never existed.

Observe how they proceed,
and you shall know how they arrived.

Planning difficulties in their ease—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The ancients used upright teachings,
easy and thus certain to succeed,
while later generations used perverse teachings,
difficult and thus certain to fail.

Doing greatness in their minutiae—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Some things are easy to do but difficult to complete,
others difficult to complete but easy to ruin.
Easy to do but difficult to complete—these are affairs.
Difficult to complete but easy to ruin—these are words.

The world’s difficult matters must begin in ease—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Men all know to discard the useless for the useful,
yet their daily lives are insufficient to complete the Dao.

The world’s great matters must begin in the small—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
On days of gambling and games, they inquire about the Dao,
yet their hearing and seeing are profound.

Easy yet not difficult,
small yet not great—
Thus the sages—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
They speak without being believed,
act without benevolence,
govern without order,
achieve without doing—
thus the heart of Heaven moves with sincere teaching,
the Three Sovereigns practiced non-action.
They never sought greatness,
and thus achieved the great.

*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The ancient wise rulers modeled the rivers and seas.
The rivers and seas practice non-action,
yet nothing is beyond their greatness—
all streams flow to them,
thus they achieve the great.

Light promises must be few in truth—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Speaking without truth,
acting without benevolence,
governing without order,
doing without achievement—
thus the superficial pretenders,
the Five Emperors and Three Kings did not sincerely adhere to the Dao.

Many easinesses bring many difficulties—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Later generations, lacking the roots of governance and teaching,
yet desiring to rule over the myriad people—
this is difficult.

Thus the sages—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Affairs are difficult to complete but easy to ruin,
words are difficult to establish but easy to abandon—
thus the sages focused their hearts on the Dao,
the enlightened saw uniquely in non-action.

Yet difficulties remain,
and thus they are ultimately without difficulty.

*Chapter Sixty-Four on Ease in Holding Firm*

*This chapter of The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* speaks:
The people of the end times indulge in perverse desires and lose their nature—
their movements are never upright.
Governance brings chaos,
self-cultivation brings falsehood.
Those who do not hear the Dao cannot return to rectitude,
those who do not understand virtue/power cannot achieve tranquility.

Human nature is originally without perversity,
yet prolonged indulgence in perversity
makes the easy seem easy and forgets its root—
thus they cling to perversity.
Water’s nature desires clarity,
yet sand and soil defile it;
human nature desires rectitude,
yet perverse speech harms it.

Knowing their own deceit is useless,
even the greedy will reject it,
yet not knowing their own desires are useless,
even the virtuous cannot relinquish them.

Thus men lose their states and die by others’ hands,
becoming the world’s laughter—
they have never failed to indulge their own desires,
thus those who act bring ruin,
those who grasp lose.

Knowing winter fans and summer furs are useless to them,
all things turn to dust and filth—
useless.

Thus it is said:
Non-action, hence no ruin,
non-grasping, hence no loss.

Its ease is easy to hold—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Wisdom discerning right and wrong
is the gateway to calamity and fortune.

Its unmanifested is easy to plan—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Movement and stillness, public and private—
the pivot of gain and harm.

Its fragile is easy to break—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Calamity’s arrival—
men themselves generate it;
fortune’s coming—
men themselves complete it.

Its subtle is easy to disperse—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Accumulating rectitude brings fortune,
accumulating perversity brings calamity.

Doing it before it arises—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Men all neglect minor harms,
easy trivial matters,
until great calamities arrive—
one must be cautious.

Later men know to respond to calamities after they arise,
yet do not know to be cautious in the subtle to prevent calamities from forming.
Preventing calamities from arising is easy,
yet applying remedies after calamities form is difficult.

Curing it before chaos—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The Dao is cautious in the small and subtle,
great calamities do not flourish.
Yet modern men do not strive to be cautious in the subtle to prevent calamities,
but instead wait for calamities to form before applying remedies—
even the divine cannot act.

Trace calamities and misfortunes to their origins—
ten thousandfold the Dao’s methods,
yet no fixed remedy exists.

A tree thick enough to embrace grows from a hair’s end;
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
A ten-foot girth begins with a handful,
from a hair’s end it grows gradually,
small things accumulate into great.

A nine-tiered terrace rises from a clod of earth;
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
A hundred-zhang tower begins below,
layered earth becomes a mountain,
subtle things accumulate into vastness.

A thousand-li journey starts beneath one’s feet.
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
A lame tortoise travels a thousand li,
one halting step at a time,
near things accumulate into far.

Those who pursue ruin themselves—
*The Scripture of the Cavern Spirit* says:
Those who love white things
consider blackness filth.

Those who love wealth excessively
do not see other things worth loving;
those who love perversity excessively
do not see the Dao’s worth.

Men of the latter age who die young
are not without arts—
their cunning is extreme,
yet the more they scheme, the shorter their lives.
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Those who love affairs never fail to meet ruin,
those who love perversity never fail to lose.
Each pursues what they love
only to harm themselves—
thus it is said: *those who act bring ruin upon themselves.*

Those who grasp lose.
*The Scripture of the Cavern Spirit* says:
Those who love black things
consider whiteness filth.

Those who love horses excessively
do not see other things worth loving;
those who love ghosts excessively
do not see the divine’s worth.

In the latter age, those whose spirits grow wrathful
are not without reverence for the gods—
their licentious rites prevail,
and the gods grow ever angrier.

*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The reason men lose their states,
die in disgrace,
and become objects of scorn for all under heaven,
is never without their love of desires—
thus it is said: *those who grasp lose.*

Therefore, the Sage of old, as *The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says,
*"If the people of this age are perverse toward gods and spirits,
who can set them right?"*

Governance lies in the Dao, not in craft;
the gentleman cultivates upright qi,
the petty man cultivates perverse qi—
hence, the Sage acts without doing,
and so meets no ruin.
He does not grasp,
and so meets no loss.
Act without doing,
and so meet no ruin—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Those who delight in licentious rites,
heedless of future calamity,
are perverse qi—
thus it is said: *without doing, there is no ruin.*
Do not grasp,
and so meet no loss—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
In the latter age, those who cling to ghosts and gods,
heedless of future calamity,
are perverse qi—
thus it is said: *without grasping, there is no loss.*

The people’s undertakings
often falter just as they near completion.
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The origins of calamity and fortune are subtle and unseen;
the petty man does not know the gates of misfortune—
he stirs and falls into guilt,
unmindful of his subtle desires.
To be cautious at the end as at the beginning,
then there will be no ruined undertakings.
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious*—*Chapter of the Talisman*—says:
States fall from losing their governance,
filial piety wanes from lacking completion,
misfortune arises from grasping action,
illness stems from carelessness—
thus, to be cautious at the end as at the beginning,
there will be no ruined undertakings.

Therefore, the Sage, as *The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says,
*"The Sage perceives their beginning and end—
it cannot be neglected."*

Desire not what should not be desired.
*The Scripture of the Southern Flower*—*The Zhuangzi*—says:
Ancient men desired,
but desired what they could not desire—
their desire reached the Dao itself.
They did not prize hard-to-obtain wealth;
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Ancient men did not prize hard-to-obtain wealth,
nor value useless things.

Study not what should not be studied.
*The Scripture of the Southern Flower*—*The Zhuangzi*—says:
Ancient scholars studied,
but studied what they could not study—
their study reached the Dao itself.

Return to the faults of the common people.
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
In ancient times, toward virtue,
they did not slight the small and so failed to practice it;
toward faults,
they did not overlook the subtle and so failed to correct them.
To aid the natural unfolding of all things,
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Ancient Sages of old
were in nature aligned with the Dao—
they knew without study,
saw without looking,
heard without listening—
the natural Way itself.
Yet they did not dare to act.
*The Scripture of the Southern Flower*—*The Zhuangzi*—says:
In ancient times, above and below alike,
there was no doing.

*The Classic of the Dao and Virtue*—*Four Children’s Commentary on the Ancient Way*—Volume Eight concludes.
Volume Nine begins.

**Chapter Sixty-Five: Ancient Virtue in the Dao**

In the age of ancient great virtue and supreme Dao,
*The Southern Flower* speaks:
The Sage did not exalt the worthy,
nor employ the capable.
Above, like pruning branches,
the people were wild as deer.

Rectitude was natural—no need to call it *yi* (righteousness),
mutual love—no need to call it *ren* (benevolence),
sincerity—no need to call it *zhong* (loyalty),
truthfulness—no need to call it *xin* (faithfulness).
They moved clumsily yet guided one another—no need to call it a blessing.
Thus, they acted without leaving traces,
accomplished deeds without leaving records—
the people were simple and easy to govern.

Those ancient masters of the Dao—
*The Southern Flower* says:
The Sovereigns of the Mysterious Age
governed with *wuwei* (non-action),
merely embodying Heaven’s virtue.

Not to enlighten the people,
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Supreme loyalty restored simplicity—
the people harbored no deceit or concealment.
Rather, they sought to befuddle them.

*The Southern Flower* says:
In the southern lands, there was a village
named *Jiàn Dé* (Established Virtue),
its people simple and unrefined—
thus, they were easy to govern.

The difficulty in governing the people—
*The Southern Flower* says:
Now, the Zhou promote cleverness, skill, and ornamental culture—
insufficient to stabilize the realm.
The people are difficult to govern
because their intelligence is excessive.

*The Southern Flower* says:
If the ruler sincerely favors cleverness yet lacks the Dao,
the world falls into great disorder.
Thus, Jie and Zhou each brought chaos—
their crime lay in their love of cleverness.
Now, the people are difficult to govern
because their intelligence is excessive.

Thus, governing with cleverness is the ruin of the state.
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Those who govern with cleverness
rely on one man’s talent—
hard to sustain the state.
If they favor clever stratagems,
they breed deceit and corruption—
the winds that destroy nations.
Thus, governing with cleverness is the ruin of the state.
Not governing with cleverness is the state’s blessing.

*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious [Original Dao]* says:
Ancients did not govern with cleverness—
the state’s blessing.

To know these two truths—
*The Southern Flower* says:
Abandon petty cleverness, and great wisdom shines forth.
This is the model.

*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Those who govern with literary cleverness
labor in vain with weary hearts.
Relying solely on cleverness,
failures multiply.
To love cleverness is to exhaust artifice—
cleverness breeds calamity.
To counter cleverness with cleverness
is like stirring water to seek clarity—
difficult indeed.

Those who know the root of governance
abandon artifice and cleverness,
letting *wuwei* transform naturally.
Always hold to the model—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Now, if one seeks to learn the Dao
without attaining the pure, luminous, and sacred,
merely clinging to texts,
they cannot govern at all.
This is called *xuán dé* (Mysterious Virtue).

*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Ancient Sages held *xuán dé* in their hearts,
and their transformations moved like spirits.
Only those who harmonize with the Great Unity
and naturally respond can govern—
this is called *xuán dé*.
Mysterious Virtue is profound and vast—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious [Natural Dao]* says:
Ancient Sages preserved themselves with Heaven and Earth,
upright in cultivating the Dao.
The deeper the human path, the deeper the virtue;
the deeper the virtue, the more complete the achievements—
this is called *xuán dé*, profound and vast.
They inverted with things—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Their inversion with things was complete.

The Commentary says:
*"Long处* (prolonged) yet not *zhì* (wise/knowing), hence it is called *fǎn* (inversion).
Then it reaches *Dà Shùn* (Great Harmony).

*The Scripture of the South (Zhuangzi)* says:
When harmonizing with Heaven and Earth, their unity is seamless,
like the simplicity of the foolish and the dimness of the ignorant—
this is called *Mysterious Virtue*, in accord with *Great Harmony*.

**Chapter 66: The King of All Valleys (Jiānghǎi as King)**
This chapter of *The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* states:
In the ancient times, the Sage-Kings governed through the Dao/Way,
retiring yet without absence, modeling themselves after the rivers and seas—
not claiming greatness for themselves, their virtue naturally manifesting,
so they could establish their kingship.

Human nature and disposition
submit to virtue, not to force.
Virtue lies in yielding, not in contention—
thus the ancient Sage-Kings,
who wished to be honored by others, first honored others themselves;
who wished to be revered by others, first revered others;
who wished to overcome others, first made themselves weak;
who wished to be humble before others, first humbled themselves.

Thus high and low, reverence and humility,
the Dao/Way governs them—
speaking gently to others while placing themselves last,
so the world finds joy in promoting them without weariness,
and in bearing them without resentment—
this is virtue abundant and *qi* in harmony.

Thus knowing to yield is to take,
and to retreat is to lead—
this is near to the Dao/Way.

Virtue bestowed upon the world,
preserved through yielding,
was how the ancient Kings maintained the world—
thus they could endure long.
This is the virtue of the Sea yielding kingship.

**Why the rivers and seas can be kings of all valleys,**
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious [Natural Virtue/Compendium]* says:
The rivers and seas are low and humble,
yet all streams flow into them—
thus they achieve vastness.
Because they excel in yielding,
they can be kings of all valleys.

*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The rivers and seas yield because they are low,
the Heavenly Pool is the *Yuān Dé* (Abyssal Virtue),
and fish and turtles gather there.
Thus the sea does not contend with the eastward flow—
this is the utmost greatness.

Therefore, the Sage-Kings
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The rivers and seas occupy the Earth’s deficiencies,
so the world submits to and venerates them.
The Sage-Kings who practice humility, modesty, and yielding words—
this is seen as yielding.
Seen as yielding, thus they attain their loftiness;
the arrogant cannot stand.

*The Scripture of the South (Zhuangzi)* says:
Once upon a time, Yao and Shun yielded yet became emperors,
Tang and Wu contended yet became kings,
and the Duke of Bai contended yet perished.
To ascend over others, one must speak gently to them,
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious [Virtue/Compendium]* says:
To ascend over others,
one must necessarily speak gently to them.
The world must imitate their joy and love,
all must promote and yield.

To lead others, one must place oneself last,
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
To lead others,
one must necessarily place oneself last.
The world advances their benevolence and righteousness,
and there is no harsh *qi*.
Thus, though they occupy the highest position, others do not resent them,
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious [Dao/Way Origins]* says:
Thus, though they occupy the highest position, others do not resent them,
and though they stand foremost, others do not harm them—
the world submits to them, and the wicked fear them.
Though they stand foremost, others do not harm them.
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
To occupy the highest position while the people do not resent,
and to stand foremost while others do not harm—
even in distant lands and alien customs,
where maggots fly and worms writhe,
all are drawn to love them.
Thus the world finds joy in promoting them without weariness.
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Thus the world finds joy in promoting them without weariness,
without them, nothing is left undone,
without their leading, nothing fails to succeed—
hence they are held in highest esteem by the world.
Because they do not contend,
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious [Natural Virtue]* says:
The ancient skilled in ruling modeled themselves after the rivers and seas—
low and yielding, not contending.
All streams flow into them,
so none can contend with them.
Thus the Dao/Way does not stand upon strength and arms,
but upon the world’s promotion of them—
not upon their own seizing.
Because they do not contend,
none can contend with them.
Thus the world cannot contend with them.
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The Way of ordinary people is many and does not unite,
the Way of the Sage-Kings is humble yet none can surpass it.
Because they do not contend with all things,
the world cannot contend with them.

**The World All Praises (Chapter 67)**
This chapter of *The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* states:
The Dao/Way is simple yet expansive,
mysterious yet luminous,
soft yet strong—
containing yin and emitting yang,
and thus manifesting the three brilliances.

The sun and moon move through it,
mountains rise through it,
the abyss deepens through it,
birds fly through it,
beasts run through it,
the qilin roams through it,
and the phoenix soars through it.

To take reverence through humility,
to take survival through extinction,
to take precedence through retreat.

The first is *cí* (compassion),
the second is *jiǎn* (frugality),
the third is not daring to lead the world.

The ancient Sage-Kings preserved softness and did not grow rigid,
retired yet were not absent,
did not dare to be proud or extravagant—
their virtue naturally transformed,
so they could establish their kingship.
They could endure long,
and their three treasures were vast and expansive.

The world all praises my Dao/Way as great,
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
My Dao/Way is *wu wéi* (non-action),
and I do not privately receive what is unworthy.
It seems not to conform.
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
My virtue contains simplicity,
yet it tolerates the unworthy.
Only because it is great,
does it seem not to conform.
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The ancient skilled in ruling modeled themselves after the rivers and seas—
*wu wéi* (non-action), occupying unworthy positions,
so they became kings of the world.
If conformity were long sustained,
its subtlety would be lost.
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The ancient Sage-Kings were clear-sighted, wise, and benevolent,
yet they preserved themselves in simplicity,
practicing non-action while the world was governed.
I possess three treasures,
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
My Dao/Way has three treasures—
to take reverence through humility,
to take vastness through frugality,
to take precedence through retreat.
Preserving and holding them.
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The Dao/Way is preserved through them.

The first is compassion,
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The Dao/Way of Heaven and Earth,
great yet rooted in the small,
humble yet self-guarding.

The second is frugality,
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The Dao/Way of Heaven and Earth,
abundant yet beginning with the few,
frugal yet self-fortifying.

The third is not daring to lead the world,
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The Dao/Way of Heaven and Earth,
leading through retreat as its principle,
retiring to yield.

Thus, compassion brings forth courage—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The ancient sages followed the Dao’s humility,
so as to place themselves below others.
Humility yields honor—
this is the fulfillment of Heaven’s Way.

Frugality brings forth vastness—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The ancient sages followed the Dao’s frugality,
so as to begin with little.
Frugality yields abundance—
this is the fulfillment of Heaven’s Way.

Not daring to lead the world,
thus one attains the completion of great instruments and long reigns—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The ancient sages followed the Dao’s retreat,
so as to place themselves behind others.
Retreat yields precedence—
this is the fulfillment of Heaven’s Way.

Now, abandoning compassion and courage—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Men of the latter age love strength and hate weakness,
yet they do not know their loss—
the overbearing perish.

Abandoning frugality and vastness—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Men of the latter age love extravagance and hate frugality,
yet they do not know their loss—
the proud and wasteful perish.

Abandoning retreat and precedence—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Men of the latter age love to lead and hate to follow,
yet they do not know their loss—
those who contend for precedence are undone.
Death is near—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The root of reckless strength lies in humility and weakness;
the root of vast utility lies in frugality and restraint;
the root of striving for precedence lies in modesty and retreat.
When these three are lost, states perish and fall.

Compassion—
in war, it brings victory—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The Dao does not conquer through strength,
but through the world’s spontaneous submission,
not through self-assertion.
Softness and weakness prevail.

In defense, it makes firm—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
High walls and deep moats are insufficient for true defense.
The skillful guardian needs no walls.
Heaven will protect it—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
Heaven’s Way diminishes the full and benefits the few.
*The Scripture of the Cavern Spirit* says:
When virtue and Dao flourish, spirits and gods assist—
this is the mark of the virtuous.

Compassion guards it—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
In times of order, righteousness guards the body;
in times of chaos, the body guards righteousness.

**Chapter Sixty-Eight: The Virtuous Warrior**
This chapter from *The South Flower Scripture* recounts:
Wei Wu Hou asked Xu Wu Gui:
*"I wish to love the people and practice righteousness while laying down arms—is this possible?"*
Xu Wu Gui replied:
*"Your armies stand like cranes at the ornate gate,
your formations do not rely on swift horses at the hallowed hall—
how can this be called laying down arms?
In ancient times, there was no storing of weapons for gain,
no outwitting others through cleverness,
no defeating others through schemes,
no conquering others through war.
Now, those who slaughter the people and seize their lands,
to nourish their own harmony and spirits—
who among them knows the art of war?
Where lies victory?
If you cannot cease, then cultivate sincerity within your breast,
responding to Heaven and Earth’s effortless nature without resistance.
When the people die, they are already freed—
what use is there in laying down arms?
The ancient virtuous warriors were not martial,
the skilled fighters did not rage.
Using the worthy without contention,
the world attains great peace.

The virtuous warrior is not martial—
*The Scripture of the Cavern Spirit* says:
Armor and weapons are insufficient for strength.

The skilled fighter does not rage—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The ancient masters of war stored their anger;
when anger was stored, their威 *wei* could be established.

The one who bests enemies does not contend—
*The Scripture of Penetrating the Mysterious* says:
The skilled warrior fights no one,
but rides the currents of time and follows the people’s desires—
and the world submits.

The master of men serves below—
